  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer11890060832810390659">Georgina Kincaid has formidable powers. Immortality, seduction, shape-shifting into any human form she desires, walking in heels that would cripple mere mortals -- all child's play to a succubus like her.<br/><br/>Helping to plan her ex-boyfriend's wedding is a different story. Georgina isn't sure which is worse -- that Seth is marrying another woman, or that Georgina has to run all</span>
  <span id="freeText11890060832810390659" style="display:none">Georgina Kincaid has formidable powers. Immortality, seduction, shape-shifting into any human form she desires, walking in heels that would cripple mere mortals -- all child's play to a succubus like her.<br /><br />Helping to plan her ex-boyfriend's wedding is a different story. Georgina isn't sure which is worse -- that Seth is marrying another woman, or that Georgina has to run all over Seattle trying on bridesmaid dresses. Still, there are distractions. Georgina's roommate, Roman, is cluttering her apartment with sexual tension. Then there's Simone, the new succubus in town, who's intent on corrupting Seth.<br /><br />But the real danger lies in the mysterious force that's visiting her thoughts, trying to draw her into a dark, otherworldly realm. Sooner or later, Georgina knows she'll be too weak to resist. And when that happens, she'll discover who she can trust, who she can't -- and that Hell is far from the worst place to spend eternity...</span>
  <a data-text-id="11890060832810390659" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer17059313028720863041"><i>"And when I was there and Erik sent me wherever he did, I felt…well, it was beyond anything I’d experienced. At first, I was so confused and disoriented. I didn’t get what they were saying about finding you. It seemed surreal. Then, it was the easiest thing in the world. I just looked for you, and there you were. <b> In all that space and all that chaos, reaching you was like looking into myself. We were so close…it defied physics and every rule of nature I knew. It didn’t seem real that I could be</b></i></span>
  <span id="freeText17059313028720863041" style="display:none"><i>"And when I was there and Erik sent me wherever he did, I felt…well, it was beyond anything I’d experienced. At first, I was so confused and disoriented. I didn’t get what they were saying about finding you. It seemed surreal. Then, it was the easiest thing in the world. I just looked for you, and there you were. <b> In all that space and all that chaos, reaching you was like looking into myself. We were so close…it defied physics and every rule of nature I knew. It didn’t seem real that I could be together with anyone like that. </b><br>And when it was over, it’s like I said—I wasn’t sure what I’d just been a part of. But I knew that I had never experienced any bond like that with any other woman. Maybe you’re the only one, maybe there’s another…but regardless, I didn’t have it with Maddie. She’s amazing. I do love her. But in that situation again? I would never find her. And I knew it wasn’t fair to lead her into a life without that connection. <b>You and I…I don’t understand what’s between us, but I’d rather spend my life alone than with someone who isn’t you. </b>” </i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1492087502ra/22480860.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>“You are the world, <i>Letha</i>..”</b><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ What???!!!<br>Seth, how do you know her real name?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1487801837ra/22052771.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/60981214" />
    <a title="The Flooze" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/355739-the-flooze"><img alt="The Flooze" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599955192p2/355739.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/60981214?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="The Flooze" class="user" itemprop="url" name="The Flooze" href="/user/show/355739-the-flooze">The Flooze</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/355739-the-flooze?shelf=urban-fantasy-paranormal">urban-fantasy-paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/355739-the-flooze?shelf=glutton_for_punishment">glutton_for_punishment</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/355739-the-flooze?shelf=vanquished_2010">vanquished_2010</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer60981214" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10984725623722695462">Georgina Kincaid might be the most <b>emotionally draining</b> character I’ve ever encountered. In Succubus Shadows she’s perpetually depressed--consumed with mourning her lost relationship. Not a page goes by without her lamenting the could’ve beens. <br/><br/>It’s all too much. All right already, Georgina. You’re sad. You’re aching. You’re oh so torn over your special wuv and forevah connection. <br/><br/>You’re also <b>dim-witted and a glutton for punishment</b> so I have to admit, I’m having a very hard time feeling sorry fo</span>
  <span id="freeText10984725623722695462" style="display:none">Georgina Kincaid might be the most <b>emotionally draining</b> character I’ve ever encountered. In Succubus Shadows she’s perpetually depressed--consumed with mourning her lost relationship. Not a page goes by without her lamenting the could’ve beens. <br /><br />It’s all too much. All right already, Georgina. You’re sad. You’re aching. You’re oh so torn over your special wuv and forevah connection. <br /><br />You’re also <b>dim-witted and a glutton for punishment</b> so I have to admit, I’m having a very hard time feeling sorry for you. Mostly though, <b>I’ve lost respect for you</b>. I think it happened quite some time ago, but Shadows brought the added insight that you have learned absolutely <i>nothing</i> in your immortal lifetime. You now <i>suddenly</i> realise that your life is going in circles? Well, yes, that’s usually what happens when you do the <i>same</i> shit over and over again into infinity and stupidly expect a different outcome. <br /><br /><b>And if this series is leading to the resolution I <i>think</i> it is, <i>someone</i> is getting a very raw deal (and it’s <i>not</i> Georgina).</b><br /><br />Speaking of where I think the series is headed, Shadows is yet another case of <b>Mead banging me over the head with clue-by-fours</b>. Unless she comes up with some grand 11th hour twist, this is incredibly sloppy story-telling. <br /><br />Shadows is a bridge book, setting us up for the series’ dénouement. We get glimpses into Georgina’s past in an effort to establish certain patterns. <b>The problem is that I (and most of my fellow readers) saw these patterns many books ago.</b> I didn’t need them confirmed in such a drawn-out fashion. All I <i>need</i> at this point is to know what the loophole is. Everything else has become infinitely boring.<br /><br /><br /><i>NB: Font enhancements within this review were inspired by one Shannon D. <br />(There. Stop your whinging.)</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="10984725623722695462" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9733884007924449438">I loooove this series. <br/><br/><b>This is one of my favorite UF series, ever</b>. Admittedly, the first book is the weakest of them all, while book 4 is my favorite. The plot, characters and romance get better and better with each installment. <br/><b>The love story has an incredible arc and it is absolutely beautiful.</b> You'll need to go all the way to book 6 to find out how it ends, and <b>it is utterly worth it.</b><br/><br/><b>Georgina</b> Kincaid is a great strong female character with all her faults. Her insecurities and weaknesses make </span>
  <span id="freeText9733884007924449438" style="display:none">I loooove this series. <br /><br /><b>This is one of my favorite UF series, ever</b>. Admittedly, the first book is the weakest of them all, while book 4 is my favorite. The plot, characters and romance get better and better with each installment. <br /><b>The love story has an incredible arc and it is absolutely beautiful.</b> You'll need to go all the way to book 6 to find out how it ends, and <b>it is utterly worth it.</b><br /><br /><b>Georgina</b> Kincaid is a great strong female character with all her faults. Her insecurities and weaknesses make her a better character, she is not perfect, but she is good. She is flawed and that makes her more real.<br /><b>Seth</b>, although completely outside of the guys I would normally found attractive, is also great; sweet and kind, he is a character that grows in each book, he is loyal, authentic and loves with his all being. He is mundane and so real that he is the perfect juxtaposition to Georgina.<br /><br />These books are full of adventure and fun characters, but to me, what really makes them so special is that the love story here is not just your typical romance. <b>What we have here is a TRUE LOVE kind of EPIC love story </b>to the likes of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/263894002?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Princess Bride</a>.<br /><br /><b>This is the kind story that stays with you</b>, no matter how many books you read or how many years have passed since you first read it , <b>you don’t forget this one. </b><br /><br />I completely recommend this series. <b>READ IT!</b><br /><br /><br />P.S.: By now, I have lost count of how many times I have read/listen to the audiobooks of this series. The first time, I did actually read them, but soon I knew I would want to come to them again and I got the audiobooks. They are great.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_93336818" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/93336818" />
    <a title="Leah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3050338-leah"><img alt="Leah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474253068p2/3050338.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/93336818?book_show_action=true">Mar 09, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Leah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Leah" href="/user/show/3050338-leah">Leah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3050338-leah?shelf=adult-lit">adult-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3050338-leah?shelf=m-f">m-f</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3050338-leah?shelf=love-triangle-love-v">love-triangle-love-v</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3050338-leah?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer93336818&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer93336818" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11160138900781866118">Georgina Kincaid is Seattle's resident succubus, and her life has been going from bad to worse lately. At this point in time, she is faced with the marriage of her best friend to the man she loves, and an eerie "siren song" is calling to Georgina, begging her to come into it. Also, amid these disasters, Georgina is still getting used to everyday life with her new roommate, Jerome's sociopathic, nephilim son, Roman. On top of that, a visiting succubus, Simone, is in town and doing everything she </span>
  <span id="freeText11160138900781866118" style="display:none">Georgina Kincaid is Seattle's resident succubus, and her life has been going from bad to worse lately. At this point in time, she is faced with the marriage of her best friend to the man she loves, and an eerie "siren song" is calling to Georgina, begging her to come into it. Also, amid these disasters, Georgina is still getting used to everyday life with her new roommate, Jerome's sociopathic, nephilim son, Roman. On top of that, a visiting succubus, Simone, is in town and doing everything she can to corrupt Seth and his soul.<br /><br />When everything gets to be too much, and after a particularly emotional encounter with Roman, Georgina finally gives into the "siren song." She soon realizes that it was just a lure from the Oneroi to get Georgina onto the dream plane. As revenge for Georgina helping the angels capture Nyx again, the Oneroi torture Georgina through her dreams, sometimes showing her truths, sometimes showing her lies, and sometimes showing her a mix of the two.<br /><br />It is through these dreams that she is able to see the progress her friends make in finding her. And that is how she sees that Simone is impersonating Georgina to get to Seth. Jerome, Carter, and Roman learn a way that they could <i>try</i> to save Georgina. And after a particularly bold put-down to "Georgina"/Simone, Seth runs into Jerome and goes with him to help try to rescue Georgina from the Oneroi.<br /><br />Impossibly, Seth is able to reach Georgina through all the different souls and dreams, is able to save her. When she comes out, she doesn't remember anything about her life as Georgina but it eventually starts coming back to her. After sleeping for three days, she now remembers everything.<br /><br />A little while later, Maddie comes over in tears saying that Seth broke off their engagement. And that he has disappeared. After brining Maddie over to Doug's house, Georgina goes over to Seth's brother's house. They don't know where he is either. As she is leaving, Brandy tells Georgina that Andrea, Seth's sister-in-law, has cancer. Upon hearing this, Georgina goes to Jerome and calls in the favor that he owes her: Send her to Seth and give her three days with him. Four hours later, when he has found Seth, Jerome sends her to Mexico. She finds Seth on the beach and, despite Seth's declaration that he wasn't returning to Seattle, they fall back into the relaxed relationship they had while they were dating. In the heat of passion, they start to get into sex, but Georgina pulls back. She's confused and still doesn't want to hurt him. That night, while Seth is sleeping, Georgina realizes that she can't see this cynical, pessimistic side to Seth and leaves, leaving a note saying that she loves him too much to stay.<br /><br />The next day, after work, Georgina gets a call from Erik, and due to the violent nature of the call, she speeds over to his shop. Where she finds the inside of the store destroyed, the windows broken, and Erik, bloody and broken, behind the counter. Georgina does everything she can to save him but they both know that it's too late. He entreats her for a kiss, giving him a painless death as she sucks the rest of his soul out of him. Before he dies, though, he tells her something shocking: There is nothing wrong with her contract, but there are <i>two</i> contracts, and he makes her promise to find the second one.<br /><br />After finding no sympathy from Jerome, she goes home, where Roman has more bad news for her. The first thing is a letter from Seth saying that she made him realize that he needed to stop putting himself first and focus on his family, because they need him right now, and that he had returned to Seattle. The second was a magazine. A magazine in which there was a picture of her and Seth kissing on the beach, the day after he broke up with Maddie. When she goes into the bookstore the next day, all her coworkers treated her with disdain and antipathy, and she has a confrontation with Maddie, during which Georgina reveals that she and Seth had dated before he started dating Maddie. After that encounter, she feels beaten down. Then Carter appears and, though he won't tell her what's up with the two contracts, he instills the hope in her that anything is possible.<br /><br />Later that night, with Carter's words still ringing in her ears, Georgina makes a decision. Seth would give anything to be with her and so she could do no less for him. That decision made, she goes over to Seth's condo and she tells him her revelation and that she'll never leave him again. They finally have sex while she is a succubus and he tells her that the side effects were worth the experience. As he drifts to sleep, he calls Georgina by her human name, leaving her with more questions and worries than answers and comforts.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />As always, I was thoroughly entertained by Georgina. While, admittedly, she had a bad time of it for most of the book, that did not lessen Georgina's sarcasm, wit, and charm. I enjoyed seeing her relationships with those around her grow, or decline as it were, throughout the book, particularly her relationship with Roman and Seth. As per usual, Georgina was faced with many obstacles in this book, and I admired her perseverance and determination to find answers.<br /><br />I discovered as a result of reading Succubus Heat that I have a thing for Roman, the sociopathic nephilim. So, I enjoyed getting to see quite a bit of him in this book. Like with Georgina's relationships, I enjoyed seeing Roman grow from dispassionate roommate into a caring, considerate friend who would still risk it all just to be with the woman he loves. I hurt for him in the end when Georgina went to Seth, but I knew all along that it wasn't meant to be with her and Roman, and I really wouldn't have had it any other way.<br /><br />Seth, oh Seth. I continue to love Seth and his devotion to those he loves, but I was also a little disappointed alongside Georgina to see that he initially ran away from his problems. However, that hasn't affected my overall opinion of him and the fact that he ultimately returned certainly helped the situation. With regards to Seth, though, I am thoroughly convinced that he is Kyriakos reincarnated. Certain comments that he made certainly support the theory, and his calling Georgina by her human name drives the theory home for me, if nothing else. That being said, I am really intrigued by how that is going to affect Georgina's future.<br /><br />This is probably really horrible for me to say, but I am so glad that Seth and Maddie finally broke up. He was never meant to be with her, should always have been with Georgina. And, while I can appreciate Maddie's pain over the situation, I won't shed any tears over the break-up.<br /><br />I really hated that Simone bitch, and I wanted to kill her when she was impersonating Georgina to get to Seth. I was very glad when Seth finally figured out there was something up (with the help of his niece Kayla), and was frustrated by the fact that Georgina never mentioned the fact that Simone/"Kelly" was a succubus so that Seth was aware of the fact. I suspect that I should have known from the beginning that Simone was there because of Niphon to fuck with Georgina as opposed to spying on Jerome.<br /><br />I continue to love and adore Carter, my sexy angel. His presence in these books always makes me smile, and I really like how he seems to care the most about Georgina and helps her out and watches out for her. Keep being an adorable badass, Carter!<br /><br />Jerome I have always loved but he grated on my nerves a bit in this book. His callous disregard for certain situations and the people Georgina cared about and wanted to protect started to affect and bother me a bit more in this book than the others. Maybe because he had more of a presence in this book than any of the others, but I really hope these semi-negative feels for Jerome do not exist after I read the next book.<br /><br />Erik, the poor thing, is dead! I've always liked Erik and I was so sad to find that someone murdered him. And I can't wait until Georgina starts solving the mystery of his death.<br /><br />Cody, the cutie, has a girlfriend! He's so adorable and I liked seeing him have this crush and start talking to girls other than Georgina! He finally started coming into his own and that was a nice change.<br /><br />Gah, those Oneroi were horrible! And the way they tortured Georgina...<br /><br />It was very interesting to see all those different dreams and flashbacks of Georgina's past. They certainly gave more insight into Georgina as a person and why she is the way she is. And, going along with my theory of Seth being Kyriakos reincarnated, I think that all the males they showed her loving was Kyriakos in a different form. It's obvious that she only loved one man in each "lifetime," so who's to say that it isn't Kyriakos' soul in another form?<br /><br />First we thought there was a problem with Georgina's contract, and now we find out that there's...two? Yeah, that's an interesting plot twist and I can't wait to see how that plays out in the next book<br /><br /><br /><br />There is something about this series that has always called to something deep in me, and think that this book has done so even more the previous four. I'm not exactly sure why, whether it is Georgina's desperation to have a human life despite being a succubus or something else. Succubus Shadows, more so than the others, appealed to this thing inside. This time, I'm sure it's the fact that Georgina was finally shown the complete dream of her life, revealing Seth as the man she would love, marry, and have a daughter with, and her pain at the impossibility of the dream. Everyone has hopes and dreams for their life, and are often faced with the prospect of failure when it comes to these dreams. But, it's something that Carter said to Georgina at the end of the book that gives me the faith I need to continue dreaming about a good life for myself:<br /><br /><i>"All things are possible. And I don't mean that as a cliché. It's true. Mortals and mortals-turned-immortals don't always believe that--which is why Hell has such a foothold in the world. And I'm not saying that if you believe in it, it</i> will <i>happen. Things don't always turn out for the best, but miracles are real, Georgina. You've just got to lift yourself out of the muck to make them. You've got to take the chance."<br /><br />"Easy for you to say. Can</i> you <i>make miracles?"<br /><br />"I try," he said. "I try. Will you?"</i><br /><br />Will you? Will you have faith that anything is possible?</span>
  <a data-text-id="11160138900781866118" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_53812197" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/53812197" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/53812197?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of Georgina Kincaid</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=2011">2011</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer53812197" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17677895962940678926">"Succubus Shadows" is, I think, my least favorite Georgina Kincaid book to date. It's not really bad, but compared to previous installments it is rather dull, it is not a supernatural mystery, as previous installments were, but supernatural chick lit/melodrama.<br/><br/>Georgina is depressed and down most of the time. She is compelled to help Maddie to plan her wedding with Seth, the man she loves. On top of it, a new visiting succubus in town is trying to seduce Seth and taint his soul even more. Even he</span>
  <span id="freeText17677895962940678926" style="display:none">"Succubus Shadows" is, I think, my least favorite Georgina Kincaid book to date. It's not really bad, but compared to previous installments it is rather dull, it is not a supernatural mystery, as previous installments were, but supernatural chick lit/melodrama.<br /><br />Georgina is depressed and down most of the time. She is compelled to help Maddie to plan her wedding with Seth, the man she loves. On top of it, a new visiting succubus in town is trying to seduce Seth and taint his soul even more. Even her surprisingly compassionate, albeit marginally psychotic, but oh so sexy, roommate Roman can't cheer her up. Whenever Georgina is at her lowest, strange things start happening to her - she loses her memory, she sleepwalks, she is drawn to something, something unearthly, a realm of dreams. At some point Georgina is too weak and distraught to resist the pull and finally succumbs to this dream world, only to be tortured by the dreams of her sinful past.<br /><br />My main qualm with "Succubus Shadows" is that I can tell it was lazily written, that Richelle didn't quite have time to think this book through properly. Whenever she starts filling her books with memories and fllashbacks, whenever her characters acquire magical abilities of watching the events from other people's POV, I know, the author was too lazy or rushed to come up with a better idea of achieving the same ending, but without cheap plot devices. (For more examples of similar rushed plotting, see <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/5996153.Blood_Promise__Vampire_Academy___4_" title="Blood Promise (Vampire Academy, #4) by Richelle Mead" rel="nofollow noopener">Blood Promise</a> - the book where VA jumped the shark IMO).<br /><br />The first half of the story was on par with previous books. It was dynamic and funny wherever G's gang was involved. But the moment our succubus was consumed by the dream world, the story slowed down. Georgina's dreams of the past were redundant, we've encountered her experiences with good men before, and we already know that it's the same vicious cycle, no need to pound on it more IMO (plus, some of Georgina's memories were copied and pasted from Mead's previously published, obscure short story). Her other trips into her present time and involving her friends were more of a plot device to show us, readers, how the search for her was progressing. These poor plot devices sucked all mystery out of the book.<br /><br />The previous book left me full of angst and hate for both Seth and Maddie, and with concern for Seth's darkened soul. This installment never built upon this drama. The characters I despised in "Succubus Heat" were too easily redeemed, their discretions forgotten and difficulties smoothed out. <br /><br />And finally, the huge clues given in this book are VERY obvious. It seems only Georgina doesn't know how the things will turn out in the end.<br /><br />Overall, "Succubus Shadows" is a decent book, if you compare it to others in urban fantasy genre. It is a must-read for Georgina fans and a good primer for the finale. But if compared to some previous succubus stories, it lacks excitement, mystery and drama, it is a tad obvious and predictable. It could have been much better if the author put a bit more effort into it.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17677895962940678926" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_78831470" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78831470" />
    <a title="LMM" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1533889-lmm"><img alt="LMM" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393087075p2/1533889.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/78831470?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="LMM" class="user" itemprop="url" name="LMM" href="/user/show/1533889-lmm">LMM</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1533889-lmm?shelf=paranormal-pnr">paranormal-pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1533889-lmm?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer78831470" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10694975520201640961">This book just about killed me. It's brilliant. I felt like this book was almost one big crescendo. I cannot even believe we have to wait another year. GAH!<br/><br/>I am going to talk a bit about it below and I won't give spoilers. However- you may not want to read b'c I may hype it too much for you & then set your expectations too high. Although I think that's near impossible b'c if you're in love with this series, then it should just be another gold star but still....fair warned is forearmed.<br/> <br/><br/>Mead pull</span>
  <span id="freeText10694975520201640961" style="display:none">This book just about killed me. It's brilliant. I felt like this book was almost one big crescendo. I cannot even believe we have to wait another year. GAH!<br /><br />I am going to talk a bit about it below and I won't give spoilers. However- you may not want to read b'c I may hype it too much for you &amp; then set your expectations too high. Although I think that's near impossible b'c if you're in love with this series, then it should just be another gold star but still....fair warned is forearmed.<br /> <br /><br />Mead pulled off another gut-wrencher. We learn so, so much more about Georgie. Why she is the way she is, how she thinks, how she has evolved, what her motivations are, her expectations, the toll being an immortal has had on her, what keeps her going. Dare I say it was profound? Maybe or maybe not but the way it was all delivered to us had such poignancy, I was a goner. Mead freakin' nailed this. Her best work by far. This whole series blows her other two out the water. Her best quality writing &amp; thought goes into it.<br /><br />For the 1st time in the series as well, I had no idea what Mead was doing, where she was going or what the outcome was going to be. I was on the edge of my seat nearly the whole time.<br /><br />It was a heavy emotional roller coaster but Mead pulled it off so deftly &amp; with such precise words, I couldn't believe the book wasn't longer.<br /><br />I really, really fell in love with Georgie this book. My heart just aches for her. I want her character to be happy so badly. Mead really fleshed her out in a much needed way in this book to allow you to have such a deeper understanding. It allowed me to empathize &amp; feel compassion every step of the way.<br /><br />I was completely impressed with the overall plot &amp; the creativity of the concept &amp; the way Mead delivered it. It could have been incredibly confusing in less competent hands and Mead handles it so gracefully that - if you didn't know great writing, you could almost take the talent it takes to do this, for granted.<br /><br />This was also one of those books where as I was reading certain parts &amp; thinking; "Yes! yes! Finally!" Mead addressed exact concerns/issues I was having w/certain characters. She also had some choice descriptive words that were pretty synonymous w/my own &amp; I felt so frickin' relieved b'c not only did she address them, but also b'c it showed she wasn't acting ignorant of her own creation.<br /><br />It really proved to me that she crafted this series &amp; that the ramifications are going to happen &amp; if they were ignored? Well, she shows that she even has an answer for that too. So yeah - she even addresses the power of ignorance. BIG time. Ugh! Sounds so cryptic but that's all I can say w/out giving too much away. <br /><br />I can't recommend this series enough. It's hilarious, poignant, witty, sexy, sly and emotionally intelligent. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10694975520201640961" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_70719068" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/70719068" />
    <a title="Heather" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2098381-heather"><img alt="Heather" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474068564p2/2098381.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/70719068?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather" href="/user/show/2098381-heather">Heather</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2098381-heather?shelf=2010">2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer70719068" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18409449889873795923">Having been brutally let down by Mead’s Vampire Academy series, I was afraid to read this installment of Succubus. I still loved Georgia, though there was no love lost for Seth. He could have died in this installment for all I cared, though I knew he would not. But as Mead has so willingly proven, she isn’t afraid to destroy her characters in order to add length to her series, and just as I feared, she butchered Georgia.<br/><br/>This story was BORNING! Granted I gave it three stars, because even a boring</span>
  <span id="freeText18409449889873795923" style="display:none">Having been brutally let down by Mead’s Vampire Academy series, I was afraid to read this installment of Succubus. I still loved Georgia, though there was no love lost for Seth. He could have died in this installment for all I cared, though I knew he would not. But as Mead has so willingly proven, she isn’t afraid to destroy her characters in order to add length to her series, and just as I feared, she butchered Georgia.<br /><br />This story was BORNING! Granted I gave it three stars, because even a boring book about Georgia Kincaid is significantly better than a lot of the other crap being published these days, but this series has taken a nose dive. I’m so disappointed! Prior to this installment, I sympathized with Georgia, now I don’t. I thought she was funny, now I think it’s sad that after a millennium, snide humor is all Georgia has to offer. I once thought Georgia to be resourceful, now I think she must have sold some brain cells along with her soul. Georgia causes her own problems in her eternal life by her inability to learn anything! Angsting over the Succubus trying to steal Seth’s soul, here’s a thought, why don’t you tell him to avoid her? Don’t want to taint his darkened soul by doing him, how about tell him the reasons behind your non-actions and let him decide? Heart getting broken every time a mortal man dies from loving you, stop screwing around with mortal men, well, aside from the one’s you have to do. Seems like logic to me, but despite having lived for centuries, Georgia might as well be socially retarded. At this point, I feel as though she deserves to spend eternity as a minion of hell, cause the last thing we mortals need, is another idiot walking around.<br /><br />I was also severely let down by the lack of angst between Georgia, Seth and Maddie. I was so distraught after reading Succubus Heat that I wasn’t sure how my poor heart would mend. If I had known it would be such a non-issue, I wouldn’t have worried. What was the point of all that build up if it was going nowhere? That’s the equivalent of spending night after night, day dreaming about some crush that you can never have, only to get him, and discover he can’t get it up. Seth should have graveled, begged for mercy, and Georgia should have held him accountable for his shit actions. The fact that she lovingly accepts him back without even giving him a hard time makes me want to heave.<br /><br />This book read like filler. We already knew about Georgia’s past, and the “revelations” might as well have slapped readers across the face they are so obvious. Mead could have skipped this installment all together and simply written the conclusion to her series. As it were, there is one more book, but as I can already predict everything that will happen in the last book, I have no desire to read it. The best characters in this series are now Roman and Carter and I doubt they will be getting any page time. I’m marking Mead off my list.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18409449889873795923" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

She has tried to create a fresh start with a new home and new housemate. Georgina begins to hear a siren's call of unknown origins, and the lure is too enticing for an unhappy succubus to ignore. Since book #2, Mead's spiritual realm is depicted as more multifaceted than just a heaven - hell dichotomy. Georgina ends up facing something potentially worse than hell.<blockquote>

<div id="review_64464887" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/64464887" />
    <a title="Shannon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2016128-shannon"><img alt="Shannon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572638169p2/2016128.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/64464887?book_show_action=true">Jul 21, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon" href="/user/show/2016128-shannon">Shannon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=color-grey">color-grey</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=bought-2010">bought-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=color-red">color-red</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=color-black">color-black</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=demons">demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=color-white">color-white</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer64464887" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer39063360092813518">Hmm ... was it as good as I was hoping? Not quite. I almost want to give this one 3 stars but I can't bring myself to do so because there were enough really good parts for me to feel justified with the 4. I think a lot of people are going to be angry and happy with this one, and then there's people like me in the middle. I don't dislike Seth or Roman so I'll probably be happy with whomever she chooses, but I really just wish she'd choose already. <br/><br/><b>With this installment in Georgina's woeful tale w</b></span>
  <span id="freeText39063360092813518" style="display:none">Hmm ... was it as good as I was hoping? Not quite. I almost want to give this one 3 stars but I can't bring myself to do so because there were enough really good parts for me to feel justified with the 4. I think a lot of people are going to be angry and happy with this one, and then there's people like me in the middle. I don't dislike Seth or Roman so I'll probably be happy with whomever she chooses, but I really just wish she'd choose already. <br /><br /><b>With this installment in Georgina's woeful tale we do finally get some answers.</b> A lot of the things that had been hinted at throughout the series finally get confirmed, but what gets more frustrating is how new problems get added to the mix. One thing gets uncovered while another layer to the mystery that is Georgina's life stacks on top. It's frustrating and a shameful ploy to sell books which unfortunately will work on me every time.<br /><br />I enjoyed the parts about Georgina's past and when she got to spy on her friends, but some of the rehashed stories were a tad boring. I understand the reasons why they were there but when I got to that part I wanted it to be over sooner than it was.<br /><br />And a thing that really bothers me is how slow Georgina can be sometimes. A main conflict of the story, which is found on the back of the book and in the synopsis on this site so not a spoiler, is that a new succubus is in town and she has her eye on Seth. What I didn't get was why Georgina, or even one of Georgina's friends, didn't warn Seth about the succubus. He knows about the demons and angels and lesser immortals so why didn't someone clue him in? All she had to do was say, "stop flirting with the succubus stupid," and Seth would have stayed away from the beginning. Maybe it was a plot device, I don't know. But it just didn't make a whole lot of sense and seemed really dumb on Georgina's part.<br /><br />As for the other characters in this story, I love Carter and I wish he could be a bigger part of her life than he is, same with Roman. I also wish the side characters would get more time in the overall story, her friends are just too much fun and are definitely underused. Jerome is kind of getting on my nerves with how uncaring and overbearing he can be at times, but I suppose that's his nature. <br /><br /><b>I liked this book but it still left me with an unresolved feeling.</b> It's actually pretty apt that Georgina comments that her life is going around in circles, because that's exactly what's happening with these books. I was hoping with those remarks that Mead was going to bring about some sort of conclusion but things are left rather ... ambiguous. <br /><br />It really feels like Georgina is never going to catch a break and she's just going to continuously suffer anguish and heartbreak. <br /><br />Carter sums it up pretty succinctly: "Boy, things are pretty screwed up for you."<br /><br />And with the way this books ends it'll be interesting to see which friends are still left around to help her out the next time she needs it. I'm very curious to see where things go next, and I hope we finally get some closure in the sixth (and last?) book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="39063360092813518" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9565377491710917358">Warning: This review will sound corny because I can't write reviews for books I like, so it's even worse when it's about a book I loved.<br/><br/>I want to thank all my Corner friends around here who keep nudging me into the direction of the right books.<br/><br/>These books are... really something. I'm sorry, it sounds stupid, because how can a series about a Succubus living in Seattle be the best thing you've read in the past 10 years? It sounds crazy, I know, but it's still true. I've spent the past 2 weeks obse</span>
  <span id="freeText9565377491710917358" style="display:none">Warning: This review will sound corny because I can't write reviews for books I like, so it's even worse when it's about a book I loved.<br /><br />I want to thank all my Corner friends around here who keep nudging me into the direction of the right books.<br /><br />These books are... really something. I'm sorry, it sounds stupid, because how can a series about a Succubus living in Seattle be the best thing you've read in the past 10 years? It sounds crazy, I know, but it's still true. I've spent the past 2 weeks obsessing about Georgina and her life and I'm sure it will be a while before she gets some peace and quiet because I keep going over what happened again and again.<br /><br />The relationship between Georgina and Seth is so beautiful it makes me want to cry, and believe me, there were tears. I want my own Seth. <br /><br />I wish I could explain it any better (I really should start doing video reviews lol) but I can't. I'll spend the next year looking forward to the sixth book.</span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review122066750">

<div id="review_642833864" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/642833864" />
    <a title="Ash Wednesday" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10484016-ash-wednesday"><img alt="Ash Wednesday" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1379043440p2/10484016.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/642833864?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ash Wednesday" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ash Wednesday" href="/user/show/10484016-ash-wednesday">Ash Wednesday</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=awesome-heroines">awesome-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=pnr">pnr</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=review">review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=2013-favorites">2013-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10484016-ash-wednesday?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer642833864" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4311511476416984283"><b><u>02.04.14</u>THE EMOTIONAL TORTURE CONTINUES WITH BAILEY, TANDIE AND ROBIN!</b><br/><br/>Seth's favorite cake flavor.<br/><br/>Jerome's real name.<br/><br/>The joys of Pictionary.<br/><br/>This is not baseball.<br/><br/>Crying is encouraged.<br/><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“Miracles are real, Georgina. You’ve just got to lift yourself out of the muck to make them. You’ve got to take the chance.”<br/>Yes, I was definitely getting a cigarette after this. Carter probably had one on him. I gave him as much of a smile as I could muster. “Easy for you to say. Can you make miracles?”<br/>“I try</blockquote></b></i></span>
  <span id="freeText4311511476416984283" style="display:none"><b><u>02.04.14</u>THE EMOTIONAL TORTURE CONTINUES WITH BAILEY, TANDIE AND ROBIN!</b><br><br>Seth's favorite cake flavor.<br><br>Jerome's real name.<br><br>The joys of Pictionary.<br><br>This is not baseball.<br><br>Crying is encouraged.<br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>“Miracles are real, Georgina. You’ve just got to lift yourself out of the muck to make them. You’ve got to take the chance.”<br>Yes, I was definitely getting a cigarette after this. Carter probably had one on him. I gave him as much of a smile as I could muster. “Easy for you to say. Can you make miracles?”<br>“I try,” he said. “I try. Will you?”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br>=============================<br><br><i>
  <b>4.5 STARS</b>
</i><br><br>Because I read this in a day.<br><br>A day may come when all this intense, voracious reading coupled with peaks in my adrenaline will lead to a yet-to-be-named syndrome/disease and I'd look fondly back to these consecutive days and nights when I was so invested in Georgina and Seth's well-being and.. still regret nothing.<br><br>Even if by then we could just download books in our brains with the click of a button.<br><br>Seeing that everyone seems to feel lukewarm to pleasantly toasty towards this installment, I'm going to join the happy crowd. See that over-caffeinated girl who needs a shower and bloodshot eyes? Yep, that's me.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380425591i/849507.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So we're back in Seattle, watching Georgina multitasking again: bookstore manager, wedding planner, succubus oh and being fate's favorite punching bag. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380425591i/849508.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm quite pleased with the direction this book took because personally, I wouldn't have lasted if it was pages and pages of planning that wedding. I liked how this was different from the other books in that Georgina was directly involved in the conflict rather than scampering around looking for answers. Because I think I've been complaining about the heavy handedness in the foreshadowing and the boulder-sized bread crumbs that leads us to who's conspiring with who to create shenanigans. It's nice to see a good dose of scenes letting me know Georgina a little better instead of trying to keep my interest in a mystery that's not even a mystery at all.<br><br>This of course was a little darker seeing as we delve deeper into Georgina's <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[and to some extent, I'm guessing, Seth's <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> pasts which was always interesting for me even in the past books. It's what made her a richly defined, more complex heroine. It's her memories and dreams that make something inside of me twinge with a compassionate ache whenever she gets hurt (and by God did I hurt for her here!) and exalt in joy when something good happens to her.<br><br>The red herrings and the misleads could have been parsed better because now that I'm looking back it felt a bit winded. But I still enjoyed the lighter fare that was more predominant in the earlier books but had to give way to the heavier themes as the plot grows more intense.<br><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>"I think that was the best show I've ever seen," said Cody nobly.<br>Gabrielle clutched his sleeve and his eyes widened, "I know! Which was your favorite song?"<br>Silence.<br>"Mine was that one here they kept saying 'My Armageddon scales will burn your post office'," said Seth deadpan.<br>"Oh yeah. That's one of their greatest," she said. "It's called 'Plywood Fuck'."</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br>Looking forward to the re-read... <b>NOT LOOKING FORWARD TO THE MASSIVE HANGOVER I'D SOON BE FACING.</b> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380401940ra/780721.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_90976367" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/90976367" />
    <a title="Penny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/679025-penny"><img alt="Penny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1323234939p2/679025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/90976367?book_show_action=true">Feb 22, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Penny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Penny" href="/user/show/679025-penny">Penny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of the Georgina Kincaid series</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/679025-penny?shelf=disappointing">disappointing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/679025-penny?shelf=reviewed-books">reviewed-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/679025-penny?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer90976367" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6266430383042928712">Reading it again in preparation for the sixth book. Observations this time around? Georgina is a major hypocrite and not nearly as likeable as I remember her to be. Also, Richelle Mead needs to figure out how to write a less-selfish character. <br/><br/>Rose Hathaway = Georgina Kinkaide <br/><br/>Also, I sort of hope Seth dies. (Actually, I don't sort of hope it. I totally hope he dies. I hate Richelle Mead for writing a such a despicable set of lovers)<br/><br/>---<br/> <br/>Richelle Mead is a very talented writer. Her books have sol</span>
  <span id="freeText6266430383042928712" style="display:none">Reading it again in preparation for the sixth book. Observations this time around? Georgina is a major hypocrite and not nearly as likeable as I remember her to be. Also, Richelle Mead needs to figure out how to write a less-selfish character. <br /><br />Rose Hathaway = Georgina Kinkaide <br /><br />Also, I sort of hope Seth dies. (Actually, I don't sort of hope it. I totally hope he dies. I hate Richelle Mead for writing a such a despicable set of lovers)<br /><br />---<br /> <br />Richelle Mead is a very talented writer. Her books have solid characters, creative storylines and interesting plot twists. I like her books. They amuse me, entertain me. That being said--after reading this book--I'm no longer sure she's one of my favorite authors. <br /><br />Here's the deal, it's not like there is anything wrong with this book, exactly. Actually, it's up to her usual standards--if not better, entertainment wise. But I can't help but feel a little bit disappointed and more then a little ripped off. <br /><br />I'm disappointed because, as far as I'm concerned, the hints Ms. Mead puts out there are about as subtle as a nuclear bomb being detonated. I just didn't want to believe it until now--because, seriously, they're just so blatantly <i>in your face</i> I forced myself to believe they were red-herrings planted to throw us off. Because of these 'hints' it turns out I've known--or rather, strongly suspected--the "big secret" of this series before I even finished reading Succubus Blues, the first book in the series. <br /><br />(By the way, the "big secret" isn't necessarily revealed in this book, but based on all the <b>obvious</b> hints peppered throughout this book, not to mention the gi-friggin'-normous doozy dropped at the end of the novel, you'd have to be extremely dimwitted not to see it.) <br /><br />I'm feeling ripped off because the series could have easily been wrapped up in this book--the fifth book--of the series. Especially since this book--while entertaining--is pretty much just filler, nothing else. I didn't learn anything I didn't already know and I hate that. <br /><br />Don't get me wrong, like I said earlier, this story is quite entertaining but very little happens to further the overall plot. Like, the progression made--plot-wise--could have filled maybe as many as ten chapters, but that's it. <br /><br />This book deserves five stars because of the entertainment factor, but loses two (should be three, but I'm feeling generous today) because of the complete and utter pointlessness of the majority of this book. *sigh* </span>
  <a data-text-id="6266430383042928712" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_145590487" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/145590487" />
    <a title="Gloria Mundi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4600483-gloria-mundi"><img alt="Gloria Mundi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312494055p2/4600483.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/145590487?book_show_action=true">Feb 03, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Gloria Mundi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Gloria Mundi" href="/user/show/4600483-gloria-mundi">Gloria Mundi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4600483-gloria-mundi?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4600483-gloria-mundi?shelf=series-completed">series-completed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4600483-gloria-mundi?shelf=demons">demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4600483-gloria-mundi?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4600483-gloria-mundi?shelf=books-about-books">books-about-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4600483-gloria-mundi?shelf=love-and-romance">love-and-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4600483-gloria-mundi?shelf=infidelity">infidelity</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4600483-gloria-mundi?shelf=what-s-love-got-to-do-with-it">what-s-love-got-to-do-with-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4600483-gloria-mundi?shelf=tstl-hero-or-heroine">tstl-hero-or-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4600483-gloria-mundi?shelf=i-can-see-your-halo">i-can-see-your-halo</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer145590487" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2233316020455899701">After five books, I find that I no longer like or have any sympathy for either the heroine or the hero and cannot face the thought of another book full of sickly sweet soliloquys about how lovely and wonderful Seth is and how cute he looks in his quirky t-shirts with his messy hair, which one might expect from a love-sick pimply teenager but not from a millenia old denizen of hell, for crying out loud. In fact, I could barely drag myself through this last instalment, skipping whole chunks and pa</span>
  <span id="freeText2233316020455899701" style="display:none">After five books, I find that I no longer like or have any sympathy for either the heroine or the hero and cannot face the thought of another book full of sickly sweet soliloquys about how lovely and wonderful Seth is and how cute he looks in his quirky t-shirts with his messy hair, which one might expect from a love-sick pimply teenager but not from a millenia old denizen of hell, for crying out loud. In fact, I could barely drag myself through this last instalment, skipping whole chunks and pages along the way. <br /><br />The shining beacon of goodness that is Seth never really did it for me (even Dante's style was more of a turn on) but now he has gone from merely pathetic to just plain detestable. <br /><br />There is no real character development with Georgina. She is pretty, she loves wallowing in misery of the o woe is me variety and she loves Seth but can't help cheating on him from time to time. There is nothing else to her and it doesn't look like there will be. The woman does not learn, despite having lived for millenia and having reapeated the same patterns over and over again the entire time. <br /><br />Moreover, it has now become pretty obvious where all of this is heading and the big reveal, when it does come, will, I am pretty sure, be somewhat underwhelming, if only for the fact that it is now at least two books overdue. <br /><br />I am undecided whether to read the last book when it comes out. On the one hand, I am so fed up with Georgina and Seth, that I really don't want to go anywhere near it. On the other hand, having read 5 of the books in the series, I feel I may as well trudge through it just for the sake of completeness so I can draw the curtain on the whole thing (so to speak) never to go back to it again. </span>
  <a data-text-id="2233316020455899701" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/169842-pickles?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/169842-pickles?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/169842-pickles?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/169842-pickles?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/169842-pickles?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/169842-pickles?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/169842-pickles?shelf=read-in-2010">read-in-2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer91320588&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer91320588" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3070456015494602627">As I finished this book, I think my main feeling was total apathy. Aside from a few parts, I thought it was capital B boring. I read all of the scenes while Georgina was trapped in the dream world and I just didn’t care about any of it. The end was a little bit better, but not good enough for me to give this any more than 3 stars...and it might actually be more like 2 1/2. I’d definitely say it was my least favorite in the series to date.<br/><br/>I think a BIG part of my issue with this book is that I re</span>
  <span id="freeText3070456015494602627" style="display:none">As I finished this book, I think my main feeling was total apathy. Aside from a few parts, I thought it was capital B boring. I read all of the scenes while Georgina was trapped in the dream world and I just didn’t care about any of it. The end was a little bit better, but not good enough for me to give this any more than 3 stars...and it might actually be more like 2 1/2. I’d definitely say it was my least favorite in the series to date.<br /><br />I think a BIG part of my issue with this book is that I really can’t stand Seth anymore. I liked him in the first two books, but it’s been steadily downhill from there. Aside from the fact that he’s a cheating bastard, he’s also a coward and I just can’t respect him. My dislike of him started when he slept with Maddie right after breaking up with Georgina - which he basically did because he couldn’t have sex with her - and got worse when he started dating Maddie, despite knowing that he’d be constantly throwing the relationship in Georgina’s face. Of course next he cheats on Maddie with Georgina, and <i>then</i> he proposes to Maddie out of guilt instead of just ‘fessing up like a man. If he would’ve told her about the affair and broken up with her, I would’ve at least respected that. I was never cool with the fact that he was marrying her just because he felt bad about being unfaithful. In the end, calling off the wedding was the right thing to do because it wasn’t fair to Maddie to marry her when he didn’t love her in that way. I felt terrible for Maddie, though, especially because I believe that if she had known that Georgina and Seth had dated (I still don’t understand why Georgina felt they had to hide their relationship in the first place), she would have never started dating Seth. She just doesn’t seem the type to go after her friend’s ex-boyfriend. And then yet another strike against Seth - and Georgina, too, actually - was that they were all over each other right after his break-up with Maddie. Georgina certainly hadn’t felt good when she found out that Seth had did the same thing to her, but she didn’t hesitate to pounce on the guy as soon as she was able. Meh. Even though I still like Georgina, my opinion of her dropped a bit this book. She just came off like a huge hypocrite and I got tired of her constant whining. Yeah, you’ve lead a miserable existence, but you brought it on yourself because you couldn’t control your baser instincts. It’s been a couple thousand years. GET OVER IT. <br /><br />Right now it feels like the only characters I still have any real love for are Carter and Roman. Weird. I still want Georgina to get her HEA, but I feel like she and Seth have a really toxic relationship and I know I’ll be disappointed if they wind up together in the last book. However, it seems unavoidable at this point, especially since the clues as to why Georgina has this “soul deep” connection with Seth were about as subtle as a sledgehammer. <br /><br />Overall, I think this was a disappointing installment in the series. This world and these characters had such potential and I feel like Mead is selling the entire series short at this point. All of the mysteries thus far have been weak and it seems like she’s been recycling the same basic plot in every book. If I’m being honest, it’s gotten rather old at this point. I’m glad the next book will be the last, since I can only see the series degenerating further from here. In fact, I think with better plotting, Mead could have made this book the finale. Ah, well. I’m still going to read the sixth book because I’ve invested the time and effort into reading the others and for the most part I've enjoyed them, but I can’t really say that I’m looking forward to it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3070456015494602627" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it

              <span id="reviewTextContainer68200809" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer958328709270236241"><i>***SPOILERS AHEAD***</i><br/><br/>Honestly, this book was going to get 4 stars from me up until the very end--although I put off reading it for awhile, completely sick of Georgina's woe-is-me schtick and her annoying infatuation with schlubby Seth. But, and maybe it was because I wasn't expecting anything from it, it was a fast, entertaining read, and I was fully prepared to give it 4 stars. Until the end. Ugh. <br/><br/>Circles...circles...circles...no shit. You're just figuring this crap out, 1700 years later? So...l</span>
  <span id="freeText958328709270236241" style="display:none"><i>***SPOILERS AHEAD***</i><br /><br />Honestly, this book was going to get 4 stars from me up until the very end--although I put off reading it for awhile, completely sick of Georgina's woe-is-me schtick and her annoying infatuation with schlubby Seth. But, and maybe it was because I wasn't expecting anything from it, it was a fast, entertaining read, and I was fully prepared to give it 4 stars. Until the end. Ugh. <br /><br />Circles...circles...circles...no shit. You're just figuring this crap out, 1700 years later? So...let me see if I have this right...Georgina falls in love with good, kind, artistic types, and it always ends bad for these men. Usually <i>really</i> bad. I'm sure Georgina, in all her centuries of wisdom, has heard of Albert Einstein? He who coined the phrase "Insanity: doing the same thing over and over again and expecting different results." <br /><br />So, my question is, are each of these men from her past, and Seth, reincarnations of her husband, Kyriakos? Or just random suckers? And to me, breaking this pattern, this circle would <i>obviously</i> mean breaking her pattern of being attracted to shining good artists, and maybe seeing love out there for herself with a certain slightly sociopathic nephilim? Just an idea.<br /><br />And honestly, Mead better have a crazy 11th hour twist, because if this series ends the way it looks like it's going to, she is a not-so-great storyteller, what with all the clue-by-fours being banged over my head. <br /><br />Does this woman not read message boards? Does she not know that 75%, if not more, of this series' readers <i>DON'T</i> want Georgina to end up with Seth? Ugh.<br /><br />And while we're on the subject of who we <i>do</i> want her to end up with, who neutered Roman? You don't need to write him acting completely out of character and totally emasculated to get across the idea to us stupid readers that he still has feeling for Georgina. Or maybe Mead <i>does</i> read message boards, and she's trying to make us not like Roman anymore? Hmmm...</span>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText13008503922673501512" style="display:none"> <br />I am seriously loving the audio for this series. Elisabeth Rodgers is rocking the hell out of the narration. She really does deserve a huge amount of credit for pulling me into the story so deeply. I just miss having the ability to highlight, because believe me, there would be a lot of it.<br /><br />The plot thickens! Some crazy stuff goes down as we head into the homestretch of the series. This book doesn’t have as many different storylines going on at once, but there’s still so much that happens. Everything is starting to pull together now, and is it ever exciting!<br /><br />There are so many great characters in this series, and my love for them continues to grow. Of course Georgina is freaking amazing, but her group of friends really shine too. I adore Carter and get a kick out of him, but I’m still trying to fully figure him out. I know he knows what’s going on, but just like Georgina, wonder about his interest in her and Seth. Doug is still one of my favorites, I just love the dynamic he and Georgie have.<br /><br /><strong>Succubus Shadows </strong>is definitely an emotional rollercoaster at times, taking my heart from achy to elated. I can’t wait to see how everything will fall in to place in the final book.</span>
